the application has failed to initializeprpoerly oxc000022 - Microsoft Community

matmeg say:

the application has failed to initializeprpoerly oxc000022

iinstalled a business card application and keep getting this message

mouneshwar r say: Hi matmeg,

Welcome to Microsoft Answers!

This error message means that the user concerned doesn't have read access to some system file required by the application. But it can occur if read access is not permitted for any DLL, OCX or other component used by the application. It usually only occurs if the software components have been manually copied to the application folder or Windows System folder instead of being installed using the Setup program provided by the application developer.

  •        What is the name of the Business Card application?
  •        Do you get this error message when you logon to the computer or when you try to run the business card application?
  •        Do you receive the error message if you boot the computer in Safe mode?
  •        What happens when you try to run the application in the compatibilty mode?
  •        Did you try running the application in administrator mode?

Here are some steps that you can try.

Scenario 1: If you’re getting the error message when you try to run the application, then try running the application in Administrator mode.

Right click on the application and click on run as administrator. Check if you receive any error message.

 
Scenario 2: If you’re receiving the error message as soon as you login to the computer, then try the steps below.

The permissions aren't setup properly on MSVBVM60.DLL in your Windows System32 folder.

   1. Click on Start; then click on Computer. Go to SYSTEM32 folder
   2. Locate the MSVBVM60.DLL file and right click on it, and select Properties
   3. Go to the Security Tab
   4. Click on Add. Type Everyone and hit OK
   5. Back at the Permission form, make sure Everyone is assigned Read & Execute permissions
   6. Click OK

Check if this works. If not try the steps below

Uninstall the Business Card application

I would suggest you to uninstall the application from the Programs and Features. Restart the computer once  you uninstall the application and check if you get the error message.

If you’re unable to uninstall the application, you can use the Windows Installer Cleanup Utility to remove the application completely from the computer.

Visit the link below to download and install the Windows Installer Cleanup Utility.

http://support.microsoft.com/kb/290301


Regards,
Mouneshwar R: MICROSOFT SUPPORT

Cursor keeps jumping all over; also Windows Media Player - Microsoft Community

rks3451 say:

Cursor keeps jumping all over; also Windows Media Player duplicated files every time played.

Original title: I have a problem with all word processing functions from Word to writing emails. My cursor keeps jumping all over the place.

Other problem programs are all word processing ones. I also have the problem with WMP (Windows Mediia Player) It keeps copying every song each time I open it. Some songs have 5 or 6 copies now. I tried the suggested solution but with no success. It seems that ever since I installed Windows 7 my computer is going wacky with a new problem each week or more. Is there some kind of patch or fix to the OS because it is very frustrating. My laptop is becoming  so plagued by problems it's almost useless.

amrita m say:

Hi,

 

Step 1:

Jumping cursor issue could be due to high sensitivity or hardware acceleration. You may try reducing the mouse setting for your computer and check if that helps.

http://windows.microsoft.com/en-US/windows7/Change-mouse-settings

 

Step 2:

You may also try reducing the hardware acceleration and check if it helps.

To reduce the hardware acceleration follow the below given steps:

a)      Right click on the Desktop.

b)      Select Personalization.

c)      Select Display on the left panel of the window.

d)      Click on ‘Change display settings’.

e)      Click on Advance settings.

f)       Go to Troubleshooter tab and then change settings will allow you to change the hardware acceleration.

 

Step 3:

Update the touch pad drivers from the manufacturer and check if that helps.

Refer:

http://windows.microsoft.com/en-us/windows7/Update-a-driver-for-hardware-that-isnt-working-properly

http://windows.microsoft.com/en-US/windows7/Update-drivers-recommended-links

 

Probably this should take care of the duplicating of songs in Windows Media Player as well.

 

Hope this information is helpful.

Amrita M

Microsoft Answers Support Engineer

Does NTFS cluster size limit partition size? - Microsoft Community

achlebek say:

Does NTFS cluster size limit partition size?

Is there a maximum partition size limit for partitions with clusters size smaller than 4KB? For example, if I'd want to use 2KB cluster size, can I use it on, say, 80GB partition? Or will there occur file-system corruption?
john john __ say:

On 8/25/2010 4:54 AM, achlebek wrote:

Is there a maximum partition size limit for partitions with clusters
size smaller than 4KB? For example, if I'd want to use 2KB cluster
size, can I use it on, say, 80GB partition? Or will there occur
file-system corruption?

In theory the maximum NTFS volume size is 4,294,967,295 clusters, unlese you are using GPT disks (which Windows XP 32-bit can't use) you will hit MBR (partition table) limitations of 2 terabytes before you hit the maximum NTFS volume size.  The MBR partition table can address 4,294,967,295 sectors so effectively with disks being arranged in 512 bytes sectors MBR disks are limited to a maximum size of 2TB.

Why on earth would you want to use a non stantard 2K cluster size?  I think this is just plain and simply a bad idea and that you should let the operating system format the disk to use default NTFS size clusters.

John

windows_xp,
files,_folders,_&_storage,

Need help creating my microsoft account with my normal email address - Microsoft Community

flogonuzim say:

Need help creating my microsoft account with my normal email address

Just bought my computer, created my Microsoft account using my normal email address.  Somehow, I ended up removing the account because I thought it was not done right.  I thought I could go back in and recreate my account using my normal email address.  It would not let me.  I am currently using a bogus yahoo email address that I don't use.  I've tried to create a Microsoft account using my normal email address but it says my email address is not available.  Very frustrating.  I log on to my computer with my normal email address then when I try to do anything with Microsoft, my normal email address is prefilled instead of the bogus yahoo email and will not let me sign in.  I really, really want my regular email for my Microsoft account.  Can you help me reset so I can use my normal email address?  Help! :-D

srimadhwa b say:

Hi,

 

"Microsoft account" is the new name for what used to be called a "Windows Live ID." Your Microsoft account is the combination of an email address and a password that you use to sign in to services like Hotmail, Messenger, SkyDrive, Windows Phone, Xbox LIVE, or Outlook.com.

 

A local account is an account that gives you access to only one PC. If you create a local account, you’ll need a separate account for each PC you use. None of your settings will be synced between the Windows 8 PCs you use, and you won’t get the benefits of connecting your PC to the cloud. If you want to download apps from the Windows Store, you’ll need to use a Microsoft account.

 

How to switch to a local account.

 

a.         Press “Windows + I” keys to open settings.

b.         Select Change PC settings.

c.         Select Users.

d.         On the right side, it will show your current account with an option "Switch to a local account”.

e.         Select “switch to a local account” and follow the steps to switch your Microsoft account into a local account. Once this is done, restart the computer and follow the steps to switch your Local account to a Microsoft account. You need to enter the correct credentials to complete this process.

 

 

Reply with the status of the issue and we will be glad to offer our assistance.

windows_8,
security_&_privacy,

andre for directly say:
Hi BallisticMissle

My name is Andre Da Costa; an Independent Consultant, Windows Insider MVP and Windows & Devices for IT MVP. I'm here to help you with your problem.

First, try restarting your graphics driver:
Press Windows key + Ctrl + Shift + B

If that does not work...

Press Windows key + X
Click Device Manager
Expand Display adapters
Right click the current display adapter
Click Properties
Click Driver tab
Click Rollback driver if the option is available

If not
Right click the current display adapter
Click Uninstall
Check the box that says, "Delete the driver software for this device.”
Exit Device Manager
Restart

Go to Start -> Settings -> Update & security, then Check for updates and install any available updates.

You might need to update the display driver from the manufacturer of your computers website.

If you have an nVidia, AMD ATI video card or Intel HD graphics installed, you can download the latest drivers from their website.

First, determine what type of graphics you have installed.

Press Windows key + X
Click Device Manager
Expand Display adapters

Once you have determined the graphics driver, go the vendors website and search for the driver in the download section:

Intel - Downloads for Graphics Drivers - Drivers & Software - Intel
https://downloadcenter.intel.com/product/80939/...

nVidia - http://www.nvidia.com/Download/index.aspx

AMD ATI - Download Drivers - AMD Support
http://support.amd.com/en-us/download

Some of these sites offer autodetect options.

As for Minecraft:

First of all, make sure you are running the latest version of Windows 10. Click Start > Settings > Update & security > Windows Update > Check for updates

Wait while any pending updates are downloaded.

You can also try lowering your screen resolution then see if it launches.

If not...

Could you confirm if this also happens in the default Administrator account?

Open Start
Type: cmd
Right click CMD
Click Run as administrator

At the command prompt, type:
net user administrator/active:yes

Hit Enter

Close command prompt, restart, then try signing into the Administrator account.

Still not working?

Open Start > Settings > Apps > Apps & features

rdrewd2 say:

If the drive is recognized, you should be able to assign it a drive letter using diskpart.  Open an admin powershell prompt (right-click your Windows icon, click Windows Powershell (Admin) or if you don't see powershell, use command prompt (admin) instead).

At the prompt, type diskpart and hit return.

At the diskpart prompt, type list volume and hit return.

Find your WD drive in the list (may be listed as WD drive or may be identifiable by listed size), and note the volume number.  For example, let's say your WD drive is listed as "volume 4".

At the new prompt, type It should say "volume (#) is the selected volume".  Now pick any letter not already used in the drive volume list shown in the earlier prompt. For example, let's say G is available.

Next prompt, type assign letter=G and hit return.

Type exit and hit return to exit diskpart.

Type exit and hit return again to exit powershell.

Your WD drive should now show up in file explorer with the new letter you've assigned.

How to send fax over internet? - Microsoft Community

jinga_ say:

How to send fax over internet?

Would like to be able to send fax over internet via software without using third party service?

a. user say:

Hi,

 

 

Thank you for posting your query on Microsoft Community Forums.

 

 

From the issue description, I understand that you need to send fax over internet.

 

 

1.Can I know which third party services are you referring to ?

 

 

Method :

 

 

I suggest you to use “Windows Fax and Scan” for sending and receiving fax messages.

 

 

a. Press Windows key + Q and then type Windows fax and scan in the search bar.

b.  To use Fax view, at the bottom of the left pane, click Fax.
– or –
To use Scan view, at the bottom of the left pane, click Scan.

 

 

Hope it helps. For any further Windows related assistance, feel free to contact us and we will be glad to help
